Éæ Â¼à¼ ¼Ä¾ï¨å´ ¡Àè ¦ÀåÆ ¨øÉå; ¡ÍúâÌ¨ ÀåÖïÃåàªú¨Æå´ï¨ ¼Çå ª¾à¾ ÂæÍæÆú ¨øÉå. Éæ Â¼à¼ ¢Éºà ¨Îå´ ÀÌêÉ ¼æ¾à ¨øÆ¾Éå,¦à¨ ïÍå¿Æú ¨øÆå. ¢ºø¾à ªÇæ ¾øïÆåà°ñ ¨»å¾åÆ¨ºëÄ¾ø, ï Æ¾ ªÄ¾¡Àè ÍÖªÌàÌ¾à¾ ¡ÉÊñÆú.

The most important is that we must create growth in thiscountry. Everything stems from growth. If there is nogrowth, that is the end of this country. Today we see a“human-less” growth in this country. The average GDPgrowth rate that had been there from 1980 to 1990 was 5per cent. From 1990 to 2000 it was 5.5 per cent, and from2000 to 2006 the average GDP has been 6 per cent. But,today the Central Bank is saying that a 7 to 8 per cent growthis taking place. So, this growth, has it permeated orpercolated down to the people? Sir, you and I should bethe beneficiaries of this. But have you felt that the growthfrom last year to today has gone up by 8 per cent? This isa fallacy. That is why I say that this is a “human-less”growth that is taking place. Today the GDP is roughlyabout Rs.2400 billion and the GDP is calculated on anexpenditure basis. So all we could basically say is, owingto the fact that there is heavy defence expenditure – thereis Rs. 121 billion that is coming to the economy and thatis what is creating the expenditure in this country – theGDP has gone up. So expenditure is taken into considerationwhen calculating the GDP. So at least 2 to 3 per cent plusthe tsunami expenditure that comes in shows that we areonly ensuring expenditure related growth which is havinga negative impact.

When you have MPMGs that go and bomb schools orhospitals, does that create wealth in your country? TheCentral Bank says that we have an 8 per cent growth rate,when they are bombing every single school and hospitalthat is located by the Air Force. That is what is going ontoday. The subject of defence is entirely in the hands ofthe President and the Government and we do not want tointerfere, we do not want to demotivate the forces that aredoing a brave act.

But remember that that capital expenditure was createdby our Government during the United National Party regimewhen Mr. Ranil Wickremasinghe was the Prime Minister.Those are forgotten. They talk of Millennium Cities whenthere was never such a thing in existence and then go onand on.

Today we have lost a dear Friend in this House.Mr. Raviraj is no more with us. Why? Because of theinsanity that was there. You said, “We will bringhonourable peace in this country.” ¦à ¤¼Æ ïªðÇÉ¾ùÆ ÌåÄÆ¨à¡æºø ¨Ç¾ÉåÆ ¨øÉå; ïÈà ¾àóÉ¨à É ´¾àï¾à ¾æÍæÆú ¨øÉå. ÇÇåÙÄ¾àºòéºëÄå ¡¼ ¡À´ ¡Íú ïÉÈå ºøïÂ¾Éå. ¡ïÀà ï°åàÊÀà ÀÇÇå°ÌèâÍÄÍºå ÀÌêªúÆ ¾ºàºÈà ¨åÈïÆà ¾æºø Éê¸å. 2005 ï°åàÊÀà ÀÇÇå°ÌèâÍ;2006 ÇÇåÙ. ï Æ´ Æ¾ï¨å´ ï «åº¾ ¾Éºø¾àï¾à ï¨åºæ¾ø¾à¼?¦à¨ ºÄÆú ¡Àè ¨øÆ¾àï¾à _

We must have real growth. Now the defence expenditureis what basically props up growth in this country. I am anaccountant and I only look at it from a balance sheet pointof view. At the end of the day the net asset is only judgedby what is there. Today’s growth should be increased by itspercentage to the next day. But, that is not taking place,Sir. Today every city in the country is either having earthslips, rains, floods or tsunami residual problems - a havocsomewhere. So, let us ensure that we have the correctdevelopment strategies.

Defence expenditure, as I said, is unproductive. Ineconomic terms you say “the broken window fallacy.” Whenyou break a window you replace it. Now in GDP terms thatis growth. But you have the same window that is comingback. This country has been from 1994 stuck in one place.In general terms we go two feet forward and come back threefeet. So we are on a reverse gear on an accelerated basis.It was only in 2002 to 2004 we were able to reverse thattrend. We were able to bring economic boom; we were ableto create jobs. The growth rate that was negative at 1.4per cent was brought up to 6.8 per cent. The defenceexpenditure was zeroed. We diverted the defenceexpenditure into areas of capital expenditure and jobcreation. That has been the difference.

When we take other important factors into consideration,growth has to be reflected through the Budget as I said.What are the components in macroeconomic terms thatprotect this growth? One is the interest rates. In a worldwe cannot live alone, we have to integrate with the rest ofthe world with clauses such as Article VIII that is there andin open market economies with a floating Rupee. Therefore,we have to ensure that we have a stable interest rate and aforeign exchange rate. Today we have about 2,500 millionDollars in our hands in the reserves. I must thank theSecretary to the Treasury for guiding me on certain areaswhich I also was not very proficient in. I was heartened toknow that there was 2500 billion Dollars in overseas banks,just earning the bare minimum. Where are the experiencedpeople who can ensure the maximization of foreign

exchange? Today the Yen is low, the Euro is strengtheningand the US Dollar is weaker against the Sterling Pound.There must be competent people to maximize the benefitthat comes from exchange management.

Then on the area of risk management, who are the peoplewho are responsible? These are areas that should be lookedat by a Government to protect the macroeconomy of acountry.

Today, leveraging assets is a very common thing. Whenwe say this type of thing, to some, these are unheard of.The chauvinistic political parties only like to be shoutingaround the Lipton Circus. Today, they are taking an offday and trying to show that there is plunging of assetsthat is taking place. The world is changing.

Sir what has the Central Bank done in order to protect theRupee? When we handed over on 2nd April, 2004 the Dollarwas Rs.93.10. Two years before when we took over it was,Rs.99.10. So there was an appreciation of the Rupee. Sixmonths ago, when it was Rs.101 they put in US Dollars 375million in order to prop up the currency. Whatever the amountthat was put in, it did not help. It was going up from Rs.101to 102, to 103, to 105 and today it is, Rs.110.10. US Dollars375 million was pushed in, in order to ensure the proppingup of the currency, but it did not help. But what is the costof that? If they had held the Dollar input until today becausetoday a Dollar is Rs.110 as opposed to what it was then atRs.101 - they were trying to defend the Rupee against theDollar- this US Dollars 375 million would have ensured thatwe gained Rs.3.8 billion. Rs.3800 million is almost 38 percent of the Samurdhi allocation. So one insane action hascaused the loss of Rs.3800 million. This is what the CentralBank has done. What about the private sector?

This is why the COPE last year ensured that we gavethis House the management style of the Central Bank; inthe areas of foreign exchange management, in the areas ofmismanagement and in the areas of leveraging of assets.None of them have been taken into consideration. ThisHouse has just become only a talking place, I am sorryto say.

There may be only a few professionals in the Government,but you do not need hundreds of them to run countries.Five or six can run this country. But at least listen to theprofessional Opposition that is there.

As I told, owing to the fact that we - our Leader and theUnited National Party - told the truth, we are in theOpposition and the JVP and Hela Urumaya for lying to thepeople before the Dalada Maligawa and in front of TempleTrees, are governing. That is the difference.

Then going on further, look at the impact of interestrates on the Dollar.

Just another four minutes, Hon. Deputy Speaker. I willabide by your order. I know the problem that you have.

On Treasury Bills, the interest rates have gone up from6.7 per cent when we handed over on April 2nd 2004 to13.1 per cent as of today. Inflation rates are 17 per cent to18 per cent. Now if you take that seven per cent increase,that is the cost to the Government on the public debt, whichis roughly about .075 per cent of GDP, you will be spend-ing about Rs.18 billion just on interest rates increase. So ifyou take the Rs.18 billion loss on interest rates increaseowing to mismanagement of the economy, and the exchangerate loss that has been mentioned, and add them both, thenyou have lost about Rs.40 billion altogether owing to theinsanity in managing the economy. Now this Rs.40 bil-lion has been lost owing to politicization. Rs.40 billion isalmost 80 per cent of the cost of creating the Mahaweliproject.

Then going on further, infrastructure development isbeing mentioned. I mentioned Port Development. I begof the Government to ensure that we do not spend too muchmoney on breakwaters. They have laid the foundation foran airport in Weerawila. If creating airports is to bring intourism and trade, then why not in Jaffna and why not inBadulla? There must be a basis and not a political sensein doing these type of things. There is no economic sensein what you have done.

Then on to the areas of infrastructure development, theCEB is desperately trying to generate more thermal powerby trying to create Kerawalapitiya. Today, that entity islosing almost Rs.5 million a day. Please ensure that thistype of insane action does not take place.

Subscription : The annual subscription for Official Report of Hansard is Rs. 2,178. A single copy of Hansard is available forRs. 18.15. (Postage Rs. 2.50) Copies can be obtained by remitting in advance an annual subscription fee to theSUPERINTENDENT, GOVERNMENT PUBLICATION BUREAU, No. 32, Transworks House,Lotus Road, Colombo 1. The fee should reach him on or bvefore November 30 each year.Late application for subscriptions will not be accepted.
